language-js"><span><span><span class="hljs-keyword">const</span></span><span> qrData = </span><span><span class="hljs-string">`<span class="hljs-subst">${process.env.BASE_URL}</span></span></span><span>/redeem?code=</span><span><span class="hljs-subst">${giftCard.code}</span></span><span>`;
</span></span></code></div></div></pre>
<p data-start="22251" data-end="22501">This <code data-start="22256" data-end="22266">BASE_URL</code> should be set to the live site (like <code data-start="22304" data-end="22328">https://yourdomain.com</code>). If the QR is just the code, ensure that’s fine. Also, verify the QR generation library is included in production dependencies (not dev-only) so it works after deployment.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="22503" data-end="25891">
<p data-start="22505" data-end="22758">[❌] <strong data-start="22509" data-end="22536">Email Delivery Service:</strong> The backend integrates with an email service (Postmark or Mailgun) to send the gift card to the recipient. <strong data-start="22644" data-end="22663">Live readiness:</strong> This is a critical component – if emails don’t send, customers won’t receive their gift cards.</p>
<ul data-start="22761" data-end="25891">
<li data-start="22761" data-end="23715">
<p data-start="22763" data-end="23715"><strong data-start="22763" data-end="22781">Configuration:</strong> Ensure <strong data-start="22789" data-end="22801">API keys</strong> for the email service are set via environment variables in production (e.g. <code data-start="22878" data-end="22896">POSTMARK_API_KEY</code> or <code data-start="22900" data-end="22917">MAILGUN_API_KEY</code>) and are the live keys, not test keys. Many email services have a test mode: for example, Postmark accounts start in <em data-start="23035" data-end="23046">Test Mode</em> where they only send to authorized domains<span class="" data-state="closed"><span class="ms-1 inline-flex max-w-full items-center relative top-[-0.094rem] animate-[show_150ms_ease-in]"><a href="https://support.darkroomsoftware.com/portal/en/kb/articles/using-po#:~:text=Postmark%20accounts%20start%20out%20in,com" target="_blank" rel="noopener" alt="https://support.darkroomsoftware.com/portal/en/kb/articles/using-po#:~:text=Postmark%20accounts%20start%20out%20in,com" class="flex h-4.5 overflow-hidden rounded-xl px-2 text-[9px] font-medium text-token-text-secondary! bg-[#F4F4F4]! dark:bg-[#303030]! transition-colors duration-150 ease-in-out"><span class="relative start-0 bottom-0 flex h-full w-full items-center"><span class="flex h-4 w-full items-center justify-between overflow-hidden" style="opacity: 1; transform: none;"><span class="max-w-full grow truncate overflow-hidden text-center">support.darkroomsoftware.com</span></span></span></a></span></span>, and Mailgun’s sandbox domain only sends to pre-approved recipients (up to 5)<span class="" data-state="closed"><span class="ms-1 inline-flex max-w-full items-center relative top-[-0.094rem] animate-[show_150ms_ease-in]"><a href="https://mailtrap.io/blog/mailgun-sandbox-tutorial/#:~:text=Click%20on%20the%C2%A0Mailgun%20Sandbox%20domain%C2%A0to,see%20its%20settings" target="_blank" rel="noopener" alt="https://mailtrap.io/blog/mailgun-sandbox-tutorial/#:~:text=Click%20on%20the%C2%A0Mailgun%20Sandbox%20domain%C2%A0to,see%20its%20settings" class="flex h-4.5 overflow-hidden rounded-xl px-2 text-[9px] font-medium text-token-text-secondary! bg-[#F4F4F4]! dark:bg-[#303030]! transition-colors duration-150 ease-in-out"><span class="relative start-0 bottom-0 flex h-full w-full items-center"><span class="flex h-4 w-full items-center justify-between overflow-hidden" style="opacity: 1; transform: none;"><span class="max-w-full grow truncate overflow-hidden text-center">mailtrap.io</span></span></span></a></span></span>. These restrictions must be lifted for production. <strong data-start="23297" data-end="23312">Fix Prompt:</strong> <em data-start="23313" data-end="23359">Use a verified production domain for emails:</em> e.g., in Postmark, [request production approval and verify your sending domain】<span class="" data-state="closed"><span class="ms-1 inline-flex max-w-full items-center relative top-[-0.094rem] animate-[show_150ms_ease-in]"><a href="https://support.darkroomsoftware.com/portal/en/kb/articles/using-po#:~:text=Postmark%20accounts%20start%20out%20in,com" target="_blank" rel="noopener" alt="https://support.darkroomsoftware.com/portal/en/kb/articles/using-po#:~:text=Postmark%20accounts%20start%20out%20in,com" class="flex h-4.5 overflow-hidden rounded-xl px-2 text-[9px] font-medium text-token-text-secondary! bg-[#F4F4F4]! dark:bg-[#303030]! transition-colors duration-150 ease-in-out"><span class="relative start-0 bottom-0 flex h-full w-full items-center"><span class="flex h-4 w-full items-center justify-between overflow-hidden" style="opacity: 1; transform: none;"><span class="max-w-full grow truncate overflow-hidden text-center">support.darkroomsoftware.com</span></span></span></a></span></span>. In Mailgun, add and verify your custom domain (DNS records) – do not use the sandbox domain for live emails<span class="" data-state="closed"><span class="ms-1 inline-flex max-w-full items-center relative top-[-0.094rem] animate-[show_150ms_ease-in]"><a href="https://documentation.mailgun.com/docs/mailgun/user-manual/domains/#:~:text=To%20use%20Mailgun%20for%20production%2C,Once%20you%27ve" target="_blank" rel="noopener" alt="https://documentation.mailgun.com/docs/mailgun/user-manual/domains/#:~:text=To%20use%20Mailgun%20for%20production%2C,Once%20you%27ve" class="flex h-4.5 overflow-hidden rounded-xl px-2 text-[9px] font-medium text-token-text-secondary! bg-[#F4F4F4]! dark:bg-[#303030]! transition-colors duration-150 ease-in-out"><span class="relative start-0 bottom-0 flex h-full w-full items-center"><span class="flex h-4 w-full items-center justify-between overflow-hidden" style="opacity: 1; transform: none;"><span class="max-w-full grow truncate overflow-hidden text-center">documentation.mailgun.com</span></span></span></a></span></span><span class="" data-state="closed"><span class="ms-1 inline-flex max-w-full items-center relative top-[-0.094rem] animate-[show_150ms_ease-in]"><a href="https://mailtrap.io/blog/mailgun-sandbox-tutorial/#:~:text=Click%20on%20the%C2%A0Mailgun%20Sandbox%20domain%C2%A0to,see%20its%20settings" target="_blank" rel="noopener" alt="https://mailtrap.io/blog/mailgun-sandbox-tutorial/#:~:text=Click%20on%20the%C2%A0Mailgun%20Sandbox%20domain%C2%A0to,see%20its%20settings" class="flex h-4.5 overflow-hidden rounded-xl px-2 text-[9px] font-medium text-token-text-secondary! bg-[#F4F4F4]! dark:bg-[#303030]! transition-colors duration-150 ease-in-out"><span class="relative start-0 bottom-0 flex h-full w-full items-center"><span class="flex h-4 w-full items-center justify-between overflow-hidden" style="opacity: 1; transform: none;"><span class="max-w-full grow truncate overflow-hidden text-center">mailtrap.io</span></span></span></a></span></span>. Update the <code data-start="23678" data-end="23694">MAILGUN_DOMAIN</code> env var accordingly.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="23718" data-end="23918">
<p data-start="23720" data-end="23918"><strong data-start="23720" data-end="23737">Sender Email:</strong> Set a clear “From” address for live emails (e.g. <code data-start="23787" data-end="23812">no-reply@yourdomain.com</code> or a support address). Verify this sender is authorized in the email service (SPF/DKIM records in place).</p>
</li>
<li data-start="23921" data-end="24330">
<p data-start="23923" data-end="24330"><strong data-start="23923" data-end="23935">Content:</strong> Review the email template/content. Remove any dummy text like “This is a test gift card” if present. Ensure the email includes the important info: gift card code (perhaps in text form in case attachments don’t load), redemption instructions for the recipient, and the PDF/QR attachment. For live use, also consider adding a contact or support link in the email in case the recipient has issues.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="24333" data-end="24712">
<p data-start="24335" data-end="24712"><strong data-start="24335" data-end="24361">Attachment vs. Inline:</strong> If using Postmark, note that it has separate message streams for transactional emails; ensure you send through the correct stream (default transactional). Attachments (PDF) should be properly base64 encoded as required by the API. If using Mailgun, ensure you’re using the correct API endpoint and including attachments multipart-form-data as needed.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="24715" data-end="25052">
<p data-start="24717" data-end="25052"><strong data-start="24717" data-end="24729">Testing:</strong> Before going fully live, send test emails to various email providers (Gmail, Yahoo, etc.) to ensure deliverability. Since test mode only allowed limited sending, after switching to live mode, monitor that these emails are not ending up in spam (you may need to set up proper email headers and domain records as mentioned).</p>
</li>
<li data-start="25055" data-end="25891">
<p data-start="25057" data-end="25891"><strong data-start="25057" data-end="25078">Failure Handling:</strong> If an email fails to send (API call returns an error), the backend should log the error and ideally mark the gift card as “email_failed” (with an option to retry). Currently, this might not be implemented – likely a failure would just throw an exception. <strong data-start="25334" data-end="25349">Fix Prompt:</strong> <em data-start="25350" data-end="25398">Implement a retry or alert for email failures:</em> e.g., wrap the email-sending call in a try/catch. If it fails, store a flag in the DB for that gift card (so an admin can see it) and maybe trigger a second attempt after a short delay. At minimum, log the error with details (response from Postmark/Mailgun). <strong data-start="25658" data-end="25687">Replit AI Fix Suggestion:</strong> <em data-start="25688" data-end="25891">“Add a catch for the email sending promise. On error, save the gift card record with a status ‘pending_email’ and log the error message. You can create an admin utility to resend pending emails later.”</em></p>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h2 data-start="25893" data-end="25924">Frontend-Backend Integration</h2>
<ul data-start="25926" data-end="37729">
<li data-start="25926" data-end="28172">
<p data-start="25928" data-end="26077">[✔️] <strong data-start="25933" data-end="25975">End-to-End Purchase Flow Verification:</strong> The entire gift card purchase process should work seamlessly from the UI through the server and back:</p>
<ol data-start="26080" data-end="26484">
<li data-start="26080" data-end="26166">
<p data-start="26083" data-end="26166"><strong data-start="26083" data-end="26111">User fills checkout form</strong> (amount, recipient, message) and submits payment info.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="26169" data-end="26281">
<p data-start="26172" data-end="26281"><strong data-start="26172" data-end="26184">Frontend</strong> calls the backend purchase API (e.g. <code data-start="26222" data-end="26237">/api/purchase</code>) with necessary data and the payment token.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="26284" data-end="26361">
<p data-start="26287" data-end="26361"><strong data-start="26287" data-end="26298">Backend</strong> processes payment with Square, creates gift card, sends email.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="26364" data-end="26481">
<p data-start="26367" data-end="26481"><strong data-start="26367" data-end="26379">Frontend</strong> receives a success response and provides feedback to the user (e.g. “Your gift card has been sent!”).</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p data-start="26487" data-end="26681"><strong data-start="26487" data-end="26498">Status:</strong> The flow functions in development (with Square sandbox and test emails). <strong data-start="26572" data-end="26591">Live readiness:</strong> All parts need to be pointed to production services and thoroughly tested. In particular:</p>
<ul data-start="26684" data-end="28172">
<li data-start="26684" data-end="27297">
<p data-start="26686" data-end="27297"><strong data-start="26686" data-end="26707">Data Consistency:</strong> Ensure the backend does not rely on any client-calculated values for critical fields. For example, the <strong data-start="26811" data-end="26829">amount charged</strong> should match the gift card value. A malicious user could tweak the frontend (since it runs in their browser) to send a different amount. The server should calculate or validate the amount on its side (e.g. look up a product or verify min/max range) before charging. Do not simply trust a hidden field from the form for price. Similarly, if the frontend passes a <code data-start="27192" data-end="27204">merchantId</code>, the server should ignore that and derive it from the authenticated user to avoid tampering.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="27300" data-end="27633">
<p data-start="27302" data-end="27633"><strong data-start="27302" data-end="27318">Idempotency:</strong> As noted, use idempotency keys for the payment. Also consider an idempotency or uniqueness check for gift card creation – e.g. if the same payment token is processed twice, don’t create two gift cards. Square’s idempotency on payment will help with that at the payment level<span class="" data-state="closed"><span class="ms-1 inline-flex max-w-full items-center relative top-[-0.094rem] animate-[show_150ms_ease-in]"><a href="https://developer.squareup.com/docs/build-basics/general-considerations/using-rest-api#:~:text=Idempotency%20works%20as%20follows%3A" target="_blank" rel="noopener" alt="https://developer.squareup.com/docs/build-basics/general-considerations/using-rest-api#:~:text=Idempotency%20works%20as%20follows%3A" class="flex h-4.5 overflow-hidden rounded-xl px-2 text-[9px] font-medium text-token-text-secondary! bg-[#F4F4F4]! dark:bg-[#303030]! transition-colors duration-150 ease-in-out"><span class="relative start-0 bottom-0 flex h-full w-full items-center"><span class="flex h-4 w-full items-center justify-between overflow-hidden" style="opacity: 1; transform: none;"><span class="max-w-full grow truncate overflow-hidden text-center">developer.squareup.com</span></span></span></a></span></span>.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="27636" data-end="27901">
<p data-start="27638" data-end="27901"><strong data-start="27638" data-end="27665">Post-Purchase Behavior:</strong> After a successful purchase, the system should ideally prevent duplicate form submissions (e.g. disable the submit button or clearly reset the form). This is more of a UX detail but helps avoid accidentally triggering multiple charges.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="27904" data-end="28172">
<p data-start="27906" data-end="28172"><strong data-start="27906" data-end="27918">Testing:</strong> Perform a dry-run in a safe environment: for example, after deploying to a staging or using Square’s <em data-start="28020" data-end="28026">Tour</em> (test values), simulate a purchase. Verify that the email arrives with the correct info and that the database entry for the gift card is correct.</p>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li data-start="28174" data-end="29962">
<p data-start="28176" data-end="28280">[❌] <strong data-start="28180" data-end="28224">End-to-End Redemption Flow Verification:</strong> From scanning or entering the code to confirming usage:</p>
<ol data-start="28283" data-end="28589">
<li data-start="28283" data-end="28343">
<p data-start="28286" data-end="28343"><strong data-start="28286" data-end="28316">Merchant enters/scans code</strong> on the merchant dashboard.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="28346" data-end="28419">
<p data-start="28349" data-end="28419"><strong data-start="28349" data-end="28361">Frontend</strong> calls <code data-start="28368" data-end="28381">/api/redeem</code> with the code (and the JWT for auth).</p>
</li>
<li data-start="28422" data-end="28466">
<p data-start="28425" data-end="28466"><strong data-start="28425" data-end="28436">Backend</strong> validates and marks redeemed.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="28469" data-end="28586">
<p data-start="28472" data-end="28586"><strong data-start="28472" data-end="28484">Frontend</strong> gets a response and updates UI (e.g. “Redeemed successfully” message, maybe updates the list/status).</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p data-start="28592" data-end="28639"><strong data-start="28592" data-end="28603">Status:</strong> Needs testing. <strong data-start="28619" data-end="28638">Live readiness:</strong></p>
<ul data-start="28642" data-end="29962">
<li data-start="28642" data-end="29227">
<p data-start="28644" data-end="29227"><strong data-start="28644" data-end="28672">Validation and Security:</strong> As discussed in backend section, double-check the server’s validation. Also, rate-limit this endpoint to mitigate brute force (if someone maliciously wrote a script to try many codes, the server should slow them down or lock out after several failures). For instance, you could implement a simple count: if X invalid redemption attempts come from the same IP or same merchant account within Y minutes, temporarily block further tries. This would be a fraud prevention measure since gift card codes (if not extremely long) could theoretically be guessed.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="29230" data-end="29487">
<p data-start="29232" data-end="29487"><strong data-start="29232" data-end="29250">User Feedback:</strong> The merchant UI should clearly indicate if a code was invalid or already redeemed. Ensure the backend returns distinct errors (e.g. error code or message like “ALREADY_REDEEMED” vs “NOT_FOUND”) so the front-end can inform appropriately.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="29490" data-end="29962">
<p data-start="29492" data-end="29591"><strong data-start="29492" data-end="29504">Testing:</strong> Create a test gift card (in sandbox or a dev environment), then simulate redeeming it:</p>
<ul data-start="29596" data-end="29910">
<li data-start="29596" data-end="29675">
<p data-start="29598" data-end="29675">Try a correct code: should mark as redeemed and subsequent tries should fail.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="29680" data-end="29725">
<p data-start="29682" data-end="29725">Try an incorrect code: should get an error.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="29730" data-end="29808">
<p data-start="29732" data-end="29808">Try the same code twice: second attempt should be denied (already redeemed).</p>
</li>
<li data-start="29813" data-end="29907">
<p data-start="29815" data-end="29907">Try a code from another merchant (if possible in test): should be denied (permission issue).</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p data-start="29915" data-end="29962">Confirm all these scenarios behave as expected.</p>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li data-start="29964" data-end="31625">
<p data-start="29966" data-end="30099">[❌] <strong data-start="29970" data-end="30003">Token and Session Management:</strong> The integration between front and back relies on passing the JWT with each request. <strong data-start="30088" data-end="30098">Check:</strong></p>
<ul data-start="30102" data-end="30665">
<li data-start="30102" data-end="30251">
<p data-start="30104" data-end="30251">The frontend attaches <code data-start="30126" data-end="30157">Authorization: Bearer &lt;token&gt;</code> on all AJAX calls (likely true if using a global interceptor or inserting from localStorage).</p>
</li>
<li data-start="30254" data-end="30314">
<p data-start="30256" data-end="30314">The backend correctly parses this token (via middleware).</p>
</li>
<li data-start="30317" data-end="30553">
<p data-start="30319" data-end="30553">If the token is missing or invalid, the backend returns a proper 401. The frontend should handle a 401 by redirecting to login (to re-authenticate). Make sure this logic is in place for a smooth user experience when a session expires.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="30556" data-end="30662">
<p data-start="30558" data-end="30662">If using cookies for JWT (less likely here), ensure the cookie is <code data-start="30624" data-end="30634">HttpOnly</code> and <code data-start="30639" data-end="30647">Secure</code> in production.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p data-start="30668" data-end="30708"><strong data-start="30668" data-end="30687">Live readiness:</strong> Consider edge cases:</p>
<ul data-start="30711" data-end="31625">
<li data-start="30711" data-end="31106">
<p data-start="30713" data-end="31106"><strong data-start="30713" data-end="30732">Expired Tokens:</strong> If a token expires while a user is on the dashboard, API calls will start failing. It might be wise to implement a token <strong data-start="30854" data-end="30865">refresh</strong> mechanism or at least a notification to log in again. If not using refresh tokens, a simple approach is to catch 401s and redirect to login as mentioned. Since JWTs typically carry an expiry, this will happen eventually in production usage.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="31109" data-end="31348">
<p data-start="31111" data-end="31348"><strong data-start="31111" data-end="31122">Logout:</strong> Ensure the frontend has a logout feature that clears the token (and any user info) from storage. In production, with multiple users, this is important to allow users to securely end their session especially on shared devices.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="31351" data-end="31625">
<p data-start="31353" data-end="31625"><strong data-start="31353" data-end="31377">Multi-Account Login:</strong> If you have both admin and merchant roles, consider if the same person might have both (probably not, they likely have distinct accounts). If switching roles is needed (again, probably not), one would have to log out/in. This is fine, just a note.</p>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li data-start="31627" data-end="34044">
<p data-start="31629" data-end="31984">[❌] <strong data-start="31633" data-end="31669">Input Validation &amp; Sanitization:</strong> All data flowing from front-end to back-end should be validated server-side (never rely solely on client-side validation)<span class="" data-state="closed"><span class="ms-1 inline-flex max-w-full items-center relative top-[-0.094rem] animate-[show_150ms_ease-in]"><a href="https://cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/Input_Validation_Cheat_Sheet.html#:~:text=Input%20validation%20is%20performed%20to,received%20from%20the%20external%20party" target="_blank" rel="noopener" alt="https://cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/Input_Validation_Cheat_Sheet.html#:~:text=Input%20validation%20is%20performed%20to,received%20from%20the%20external%20party" class="flex h-4.5 overflow-hidden rounded-xl px-2 text-[9px] font-medium text-token-text-secondary! bg-[#F4F4F4]! dark:bg-[#303030]! transition-colors duration-150 ease-in-out"><span class="relative start-0 bottom-0 flex h-full w-full items-center"><span class="flex h-4 w-full items-center justify-between overflow-hidden" style="opacity: 1; transform: none;"><span class="max-w-full grow truncate overflow-hidden text-center">cheatsheetseries.owasp.org</span></span></span></a></span></span>. <strong data-start="31832" data-end="31843">Status:</strong> Some basic validation might be in place (for example, checking required fields are not empty). <strong data-start="31939" data-end="31958">Live readiness:</strong> Harden these validations:</p>
<ul data-start="31987" data-end="34044">
<li data-start="31987" data-end="32404">
<p data-start="31989" data-end="32404"><strong data-start="31989" data-end="32007">Purchase Data:</strong> Validate the email address format for the recipient on the server (e.g. using a regex or a library) to avoid sending emails to malformed addresses<span class="" data-state="closed"><span class="ms-1 inline-flex max-w-full items-center relative top-[-0.094rem] animate-[show_150ms_ease-in]"><a href="https://cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/Input_Validation_Cheat_Sheet.html#:~:text=Input%20validation%20should%20be%20applied,both%20syntactic%20and%20semantic%20levels" target="_blank" rel="noopener" alt="https://cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/Input_Validation_Cheat_Sheet.html#:~:text=Input%20validation%20should%20be%20applied,both%20syntactic%20and%20semantic%20levels" class="flex h-4.5 overflow-hidden rounded-xl px-2 text-[9px] font-medium text-token-text-secondary! bg-[#F4F4F4]! dark:bg-[#303030]! transition-colors duration-150 ease-in-out"><span class="relative start-0 bottom-0 flex h-full w-full items-center"><span class="flex h-4 w-full items-center justify-between overflow-hidden" style="opacity: 1; transform: none;"><span class="max-w-full grow truncate overflow-hidden text-center">cheatsheetseries.owasp.org</span></span></span></a></span></span><span class="" data-state="closed"><span class="ms-1 inline-flex max-w-full items-center relative top-[-0.094rem] animate-[show_150ms_ease-in]"><a href="https://cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/Input_Validation_Cheat_Sheet.html#:~:text=minimum%20and%20maximum%20length%20check,as%20the%20main%20validation%20method" target="_blank" rel="noopener" alt="https://cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/Input_Validation_Cheat_Sheet.html#:~:text=minimum%20and%20maximum%20length%20check,as%20the%20main%20validation%20method" class="flex h-4.5 overflow-hidden rounded-xl px-2 text-[9px] font-medium text-token-text-secondary! bg-[#F4F4F4]! dark:bg-[#303030]! transition-colors duration-150 ease-in-out"><span class="relative start-0 bottom-0 flex h-full w-full items-center"><span class="flex h-4 w-full items-center justify-between overflow-hidden" style="opacity: 1; transform: none;"><span class="max-w-full grow truncate overflow-hidden text-center">cheatsheetseries.owasp.org</span></span></span></a></span></span>. Validate that the amount is within allowed limits (e.g. a positive amount above zero and not ridiculously high). If you expect certain fixed denominations, enforce that.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="32407" data-end="32752">
<p data-start="32409" data-end="32752"><strong data-start="32409" data-end="32429">Redemption Data:</strong> Validate the format of gift card codes. For instance, if codes should be 12 alphanumeric characters, check the input matches that before even querying the database. This not only helps security but avoids unnecessary DB hits for obviously invalid codes (and can prevent some brute force by quickly rejecting wrong format).</p>
</li>
<li data-start="32755" data-end="33122">
<p data-start="32757" data-end="33122"><strong data-start="32757" data-end="32769">General:</strong> Use a consistent approach or library for validation where possible (e.g. Joi or express-validator in Node) for maintainability. Implement both <strong data-start="32913" data-end="32926">syntactic</strong> (correct format/type) and <strong data-start="32953" data-end="32965">semantic</strong> (logical correctness) validation<span class="" data-state="closed"><span class="ms-1 inline-flex max-w-full items-center relative top-[-0.094rem] animate-[show_150ms_ease-in]"><a href="https://cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/Input_Validation_Cheat_Sheet.html#:~:text=Input%20validation%20should%20be%20applied,both%20syntactic%20and%20semantic%20levels" target="_blank" rel="noopener" alt="https://cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/Input_Validation_Cheat_Sheet.html#:~:text=Input%20validation%20should%20be%20applied,both%20syntactic%20and%20semantic%20levels" class="flex h-4.5 overflow-hidden rounded-xl px-2 text-[9px] font-medium text-token-text-secondary! bg-[#F4F4F4]! dark:bg-[#303030]! transition-colors duration-150 ease-in-out"><span class="relative start-0 bottom-0 flex h-full w-full items-center"><span class="flex h-4 w-full items-center justify-between overflow-hidden" style="opacity: 1; transform: none;"><span class="max-w-full grow truncate overflow-hidden text-center">cheatsheetseries.owasp.org</span></span></span></a></span></span>. For example, syntactic: “email must match regex”, semantic: “amount must be &gt;= $5”.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="33125" data-end="33439">
<p data-start="33127" data-end="33439"><strong data-start="33127" data-end="33144">Sanitization:</strong> If any of this input is later displayed (e.g. the message the buyer writes to the recipient might be included in the email or shown in a dashboard), ensure to sanitize it to prevent XSS or formatting issues. At minimum, escape HTML characters in that message or limit allowed characters/emojis.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="33442" data-end="33644">
<p data-start="33444" data-end="33644"><strong data-start="33444" data-end="33465">SQL/NoSQL safety:</strong> If using raw queries anywhere, guard against injection. Ideally use parameterized queries/ORM. This is more of a code review item, but mentioning as a reminder for live security.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="33647" data-end="34044">
<p data-start="33649" data-end="34044"><strong data-start="33649" data-end="33664">Fix Prompt:</strong> <em data-start="33665" data-end="33705">Add server-side validation middleware:</em> e.g. use <code data-start="33715" data-end="33734">express-validator</code> to check <code data-start="33744" data-end="33760">req.body.email</code> is email, <code data-start="33771" data-end="33779">amount</code> is numeric and within range, etc., returning 400 Bad Request with errors if validation fails. Also trim and sanitize inputs like names/messages by removing script tags or excessive length (set a max length for the message, such as 200 characters, to avoid abuse).</p>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li data-start="34046" data-end="37729">
<p data-start="34048" data-end="34193">[❌] <strong data-start="34052" data-end="34081">Error Handling &amp; Logging:</strong> In a live environment, the system must handle failures gracefully and leave an audit trail for troubleshooting:</p>
<ul data-start="34196" data-end="37729">
<li data-start="34196" data-end="35068">
<p data-start="34198" data-end="35068"><strong data-start="34198" data-end="34219">Payment Failures:</strong> If Square’s API call to charge the card fails (e.g. card declined, insufficient funds, or config error), the backend should catch that error. The API should respond to the frontend with an informative error (without exposing too much detail – maybe just “Payment failed: &lt;Square error message&gt;”). The frontend should then display that to the user so they know the purchase didn’t go through. Make sure that <em data-start="34627" data-end="34682">no gift card is generated or emailed if payment fails</em>. (From Square’s perspective, a failed payment means no charge occurred; our system should then abort the gift card creation.) Logging: record the failure reason from Square in the server logs (and possibly to an admin-accessible log). Square typically returns error codes like <code data-start="34960" data-end="34975">CARD_DECLINED</code> or <code data-start="34979" data-end="34999">VERIFY_CVV_FAILURE</code> – these can be useful to log<span class="" data-state="closed"><span class="ms-1 inline-flex max-w-full items-center relative top-[-0.094rem] animate-[show_150ms_ease-in]"><a href="https://developer.squareup.com/docs/build-basics/access-tokens#:~:text=Using%20the%20wrong%20access%20token,error%20code" target="_blank" rel="noopener" alt="https://developer.squareup.com/docs/build-basics/access-tokens#:~:text=Using%20the%20wrong%20access%20token,error%20code" class="flex h-4.5 overflow-hidden rounded-xl px-2 text-[9px] font-medium text-token-text-secondary! bg-[#F4F4F4]! dark:bg-[#303030]! transition-colors duration-150 ease-in-out"><span class="relative start-0 bottom-0 flex h-full w-full items-center"><span class="flex h-4 w-full items-center justify-between overflow-hidden" style="opacity: 1; transform: none;"><span class="max-w-full grow truncate overflow-hidden text-center">developer.squareup.com</span></span></span></a></span></span>.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="35071" data-end="35962">
<p data-start="35073" data-end="35962"><strong data-start="35073" data-end="35092">Email Failures:</strong> As mentioned, if the email send fails after payment succeeded, we’re in a tricky spot – the customer was charged and we have a gift card, but delivery failed. The system should handle this by flagging the gift card (so it can be re-sent) and maybe automatically retrying after a short delay. Many email services are reliable, but network issues or configuration problems can cause send failures. Implement a <strong data-start="35501" data-end="35520">retry mechanism</strong> for email: e.g. try up to 3 times with a few seconds interval, or use a background job queue to retry later. If all attempts fail, mark the gift card for manual intervention. This is where an admin dashboard entry for “Failed emails” would be helpful so you don’t miss fulfilling a purchase. Logging: output the error details (e.g. “550 Unknown User” or API error message) in logs and, if possible, store it attached to the gift card record.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="35965" data-end="36486">
<p data-start="35967" data-end="36486"><strong data-start="35967" data-end="35988">Webhook Failures:</strong> If using webhooks (Square or others), note that Square will retry webhooks on failure a number of times. Ensure your webhook endpoint responds with HTTP 200 as quickly as possible (within 10 seconds ideally) to signal success. If processing is heavy, consider queuing work. Also design idempotency for webhook handling – if the same event is delivered twice (due to retry), your logic should recognize it (maybe by event ID) and not duplicate actions (like not marking a gift card redeemed twice).</p>
</li>
<li data-start="36489" data-end="36806">
<p data-start="36491" data-end="36806"><strong data-start="36491" data-end="36514">General Exceptions:</strong> Make sure the Node process (or whatever backend) doesn’t crash on an uncaught exception. Use try/catch around critical sections (payment processing, email sending, PDF generation as noted). Possibly use a global exception handler or a service like Sentry for error monitoring in production.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="36809" data-end="37235">
<p data-start="36811" data-end="37235"><strong data-start="36811" data-end="36838">Logging and Monitoring:</strong> In production, console logs may not be enough. Ensure that you have a way to review logs (Replit logs or an external logging service) for errors. Remove any verbose debug logs that could clutter or expose sensitive info (like do not log full credit card tokens or user passwords). Instead, log high-level events (e.g. “Payment succeeded for giftCardId 123, Square transactionId XYZ”) and errors.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="37238" data-end="37729">
<p data-start="37240" data-end="37294"><strong data-start="37240" data-end="37255">Fix Prompt:</strong> <em data-start="37256" data-end="37287">Implement structured logging:</em> e.g.,</p>
<pre class="overflow-visible!" data-start="37299" data-end="37427"><div class="contain-inline-size rounded-2xl relative bg-token-sidebar-surface-primary"><div class="flex items-center <h2 data-start="37731" data-end="37761">Live Deployment &amp; Usability</h2>
<ul data-start="37763" data-end="45549">
<li data-start="37763" data-end="39631">
<p data-start="37765" data-end="37904">[✔️] <strong data-start="37770" data-end="37801">Environment Variable Setup:</strong> Prepare a complete list of environment variables needed for production and verify they are configured:</p>
<ul data-start="37907" data-end="39514">
<li data-start="37907" data-end="38145">
<p data-start="37909" data-end="38145"><code data-start="37909" data-end="37919">NODE_ENV</code> should be set to <code data-start="37937" data-end="37951">"production"</code> in the live environment. This can influence framework behavior (for example, React builds in production mode are optimized, and some libraries behave differently when <code data-start="38119" data-end="38129">NODE_ENV</code> is production).</p>
</li>
<li data-start="38148" data-end="38702">
<p data-start="38150" data-end="38702"><strong data-start="38150" data-end="38173">Square Credentials:</strong> <code data-start="38174" data-end="38195">SQUARE_ACCESS_TOKEN</code> (production) and possibly <code data-start="38222" data-end="38242">SQUARE_LOCATION_ID</code>, <code data-start="38244" data-end="38259">SQUARE_APP_ID</code> (for the front-end to initialize the payment form). These must be the live credentials from Square Developer Dashboard (not the sandbox ones)<span class="" data-state="closed"><span class="ms-1 inline-flex max-w-full items-center relative top-[-0.094rem] animate-[show_150ms_ease-in]"><a href="https://developer.squareup.com/docs/build-basics/access-tokens#:~:text=Each%20application%20you%20create%20in,are%20generally%20used%20for%20testing" target="_blank" rel="noopener" alt="https://developer.squareup.com/docs/build-basics/access-tokens#:~:text=Each%20application%20you%20create%20in,are%20generally%20used%20for%20testing" class="flex h-4.5 overflow-hidden rounded-xl px-2 text-[9px] font-medium text-token-text-secondary! bg-[#F4F4F4]! dark:bg-[#303030]! transition-colors duration-150 ease-in-out"><span class="relative start-0 bottom-0 flex h-full w-full items-center"><span class="flex h-4 w-full items-center justify-between overflow-hidden" style="opacity: 1; transform: none;"><span class="max-w-full grow truncate overflow-hidden text-center">developer.squareup.com</span></span></span></a></span></span>. Keep them secret – ensure they are stored securely (Replit Secrets or env vars) and not visible in client-side code. (The Square Application ID will be visible in front-end, that’s okay – it’s not a secret, but the access token must remain on the server only).</p>
</li>
<li data-start="38705" data-end="38925">
<p data-start="38707" data-end="38925"><strong data-start="38707" data-end="38737">Email Service Credentials:</strong> e.g. <code data-start="38743" data-end="38766">POSTMARK_SERVER_TOKEN</code> or <code data-start="38770" data-end="38787">MAILGUN_API_KEY</code> and <code data-start="38792" data-end="38808">MAILGUN_DOMAIN</code>. Again, use the live server/API token. Also set any other related configs, like <code data-start="38889" data-end="38909">EMAIL_FROM_ADDRESS</code> if you use one.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="38928" data-end="39109">
<p data-start="38930" data-end="39109"><strong data-start="38930" data-end="38956">Database URLs or Keys:</strong> (Not explicitly mentioned, but if the project uses a database or Replit DB, ensure the connection string is set for production, if it differs from dev.)</p>
</li>
<li data-start="39112" data-end="39244">
<p data-start="39114" data-end="39244"><strong data-start="39114" data-end="39127">Base URL:</strong> If needed (for constructing links in emails/QR), set something like <code data-start="39196" data-end="39243">APP_BASE_URL = "https://your-live-domain.com"</code>.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="39247" data-end="39350">
<p data-start="39249" data-end="39350"><strong data-start="39249" data-end="39264">JWT Secret:</strong> <code data-start="39265" data-end="39277">JWT_SECRET</code> (choose a strong random string in production; never use the dev secret).</p>
</li>
<li data-start="39353" data-end="39511">
<p data-start="39355" data-end="39511"><strong data-start="39355" data-end="39373">Other Secrets:</strong> If using any API for PDF generation or any other service (e.g. an API key for a QR code service if not generated locally), set those too.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p data-start="39517" data-end="39631">Before deploying, double-check that all necessary env vars are supplied; missing ones often cause runtime errors.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="39633" data-end="40383">
<p data-start="39635" data-end="40383">[✔️] <strong data-start="39640" data-end="39670">Production Build &amp; Assets:</strong> Ensure that the front-end is properly built for production (minified, etc.) and that all static assets (images, CSS) are loading over HTTPS in the deployed environment. Any references to local addresses (like <code data-start="39880" data-end="39898">http://localhost</code> or test URLs in the code) should be updated to relative or correct production URLs. This includes API calls – often in development you might have a proxy or use localhost:5000 for API, but in production you might serve front and back under the same domain. Adjust the front-end API base path if needed (e.g. <code data-start="40207" data-end="40231">fetch('/api/endpoint')</code> is usually fine if front-end and back-end are on one domain). Also, remove any references to development-only libraries or testing scripts in the HTML.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="40385" data-end="41773">
<p data-start="40387" data-end="40497">[❌] <strong data-start="40391" data-end="40420">Webhook URL Registration:</strong> As noted under Square integration, configure webhooks for live. In addition:</p>
<ul data-start="40500" data-end="41773">
<li data-start="40500" data-end="41103">
<p data-start="40502" data-end="41103"><strong data-start="40502" data-end="40521">Email Webhooks:</strong> If using Postmark, you can set up webhook callbacks for bounces/spam complaints. While not mandatory, it might be useful to register these to a backend endpoint (e.g. <code data-start="40689" data-end="40716">/api/webhook/email_bounce</code>) to log if an email failed (in case a valid address bounces). If using Mailgun, similarly you can set webhooks for delivered/failed events. This can help in monitoring email delivery in production. If you do set these up, ensure to secure them (Mailgun signs webhook events, verify the signature). If not setting up now, it’s okay – but be aware of this feature for future improvements.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="41106" data-end="41461">
<p data-start="41108" data-end="41461"><strong data-start="41108" data-end="41125">Domain &amp; SSL:</strong> Make sure your production domain has a valid SSL certificate (so that webhooks (and users) can communicate securely). Services like Square and Postmark will require a secure endpoint (Square webhooks won’t send to HTTP URLs). If hosting on Replit or similar, use their HTTPS domain. If using a custom domain, confirm SSL is configured.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="41464" data-end="41773">
<p data-start="41466" data-end="41773"><strong data-start="41466" data-end="41487">Testing webhooks:</strong> After deployment, simulate or trigger a webhook event if possible. For Square, you might do a test payment or use their webhook testing feature. For email, sending a test to a bounced address can trigger a bounce webhook. Monitor that the endpoint receives and handles it (check logs).</p>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li data-start="41775" data-end="42974">
<p data-start="41777" data-end="41885">[❌] <strong data-start="41781" data-end="41821">Email Sending Domain and Reputation:</strong> Now that you are going live, consider the email deliverability:</p>
<ul data-start="41888" data-end="42974">
<li data-start="41888" data-end="42178">
<p data-start="41890" data-end="42178"><strong data-start="41890" data-end="41913">Verify DNS records:</strong> SPF, DKIM, and (optionally) DMARC records for your sending domain should be in place. Services like Postmark/Mailgun provide these records in their UI for you to add to DNS. This greatly improves trust so recipient mail servers don’t flag your messages as spoofed.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="42181" data-end="42401">
<p data-start="42183" data-end="42401"><strong data-start="42183" data-end="42205">Warm-up if needed:</strong> If you plan to send a lot of emails, a warm-up period (sending gradually increasing amounts) can help avoid spam filters. Initially, there may be low volume, but keep this in mind as usage grows.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="42404" data-end="42676">
<p data-start="42406" data-end="42676"><strong data-start="42406" data-end="42433">Remove Test Mode Flags:</strong> If any code path checks for a “test mode” to, say, divert emails to a fixed address (some developers do this to avoid sending real emails during dev), disable that for production. All emails in production should go to the intended recipients.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="42679" data-end="42974">
<p data-start="42681" data-end="42974"><strong data-start="42681" data-end="42697">Backup Plan:</strong> On the rare chance the email service has an outage, have a plan (even if manual) to retrieve undelivered gift card info. For example, maintain a copy of the gift card PDF or details in the database so it can be re-sent later. This ties into logging failed emails as mentioned.</p>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li data-start="42976" data-end="44556">
<p data-start="42978" data-end="43059">[❌] <strong data-start="42982" data-end="43009">Sandbox/Test Artifacts:</strong> Scrub the system for any leftover test artifacts:</p>
<ul data-start="43062" data-end="44556">
<li data-start="43062" data-end="43334">
<p data-start="43064" data-end="43334"><strong data-start="43064" data-end="43078">Test Data:</strong> Remove any dummy users (e.g. a “test merchant” or “admin” account with a known password that was used during development). Ensure default credentials are changed to secure ones. Any test gift cards in the database should be cleared out before live launch.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="43337" data-end="43641">
<p data-start="43339" data-end="43641"><strong data-start="43339" data-end="43359">Disabled Checks:</strong> Sometimes during testing, certain verifications might be bypassed (e.g. “// TODO: skip verification in dev”). Make sure no such bypasses remain. For example, if in development you short-circuited the Square payment (to not charge real card), that must be re-enabled for production.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="43644" data-end="43893">
<p data-start="43646" data-end="43893"><strong data-start="43646" data-end="43663">Console Logs:</strong> Clean up excessive <code data-start="43683" data-end="43696">console.log</code> statements that might have been used in testing (especially if they log sensitive data). In Node, <code data-start="43795" data-end="43816">NODE_ENV=production</code> can disable some debugging, but it’s best to remove or guard logs manually.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="43896" data-end="44046">
<p data-start="43898" data-end="44046"><strong data-start="43898" data-end="43918">Debug Endpoints:</strong> If any debug or admin endpoints were added (like <code data-start="43968" data-end="43984">/api/testEmail</code> or <code data-start="43988" data-end="44003">/api/dumpLogs</code>), remove or secure them before production.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="44049" data-end="44556">
<p data-start="44051" data-end="44556"><strong data-start="44051" data-end="44070">Configurations:</strong> Ensure that any configuration labeled as “sandbox” or “development” is switched off. For example, Mailgun’s free plan without a credit card keeps you in sandbox mode (only authorized recipients)<span class="" data-state="closed"><span class="ms-1 inline-flex max-w-full items-center relative top-[-0.094rem] animate-[show_150ms_ease-in]"><a href="https://help.mailgun.com/hc/en-us/articles/217531258-Authorized-Recipients#:~:text=Authorized%20Recipients%20,sending%20just%20to%20Authorized" target="_blank" rel="noopener" alt="https://help.mailgun.com/hc/en-us/articles/217531258-Authorized-Recipients#:~:text=Authorized%20Recipients%20,sending%20just%20to%20Authorized" class="flex h-4.5 overflow-hidden rounded-xl px-2 text-[9px] font-medium text-token-text-secondary! bg-[#F4F4F4]! dark:bg-[#303030]! transition-colors duration-150 ease-in-out"><span class="relative start-0 bottom-0 flex h-full w-full items-center"><span class="flex h-4 w-full items-center justify-between overflow-hidden" style="opacity: 1; transform: none;"><span class="max-w-full grow truncate overflow-hidden text-center">help.mailgun.com</span></span></span></a></span></span> – upgrade or add a card to enable real sending. Square’s sandbox token should not be present in the prod config. Essentially, anything intended <em data-start="44449" data-end="44455">only</em> for testing should be either removed or clearly isolated such that it never runs in production mode.</p>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li data-start="44558" data-end="45549">
<p data-start="44560" data-end="44656">[❌] <strong data-start="44564" data-end="44588">Monitoring &amp; Alerts:</strong> While not explicitly asked, a live system benefits from monitoring:</p>
<ul data-start="44659" data-end="45549">
<li data-start="44659" data-end="44804">
<p data-start="44661" data-end="44804"><strong data-start="44661" data-end="44683">Uptime Monitoring:</strong> Use a service to ping the site and API periodically to ensure it’s up. This can alert you quickly if the site goes down.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="44807" data-end="45037">
<p data-start="44809" data-end="45037"><strong data-start="44809" data-end="44828">Error Tracking:</strong> Consider integrating an error tracking service (like Sentry) for the backend (and possibly frontend) to catch exceptions. This can give stack traces and alerts if something goes wrong for users in production.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="45040" data-end="45295">
<p data-start="45042" data-end="45295"><strong data-start="45042" data-end="45061">Analytics/Logs:</strong> At minimum, monitor the server logs regularly. If deploying on a platform that provides log access or an admin console, keep an eye out for errors or unusual activity (like many failed redemption attempts which could indicate abuse).</p>
</li>
<li data-start="45298" data-end="45549">
<p data-start="45300" data-end="45549"><strong data-start="45300" data-end="45326">Scaling &amp; Performance:</strong> If you anticipate high load, ensure the infrastructure can handle it. (For example, if running on a free tier, watch out for rate limits.) But if initial usage is small, this is less urgent – just keep in mind as you grow.</p>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<hr data-start="45551" data-end="45554">
<p data-start="45556" data-end="46169">Overall, <strong data-start="45565" data-end="45585">SiZuGiftCardShop</strong> is close to being production-ready, with a solid full-stack foundation. Addressing the unchecked items above will mitigate major risks and ensure a smooth launch. Focus on tightening security (JWT, input validation, role checks), switching all integrations to live mode (Square payments and email service), and implementing robust error handling with retries for critical external dependencies (webhooks, email). By following these recommendations and testing each flow in a staging environment, you can confidently go live with a platform that is functional, secure, and resilient.</p>
<p data-start="46171" data-end="46293"><strong data-start="46171" data-end="46205">Replit AI Fix Prompts Summary:</strong> Below are key fixes identified, phrased as prompts for quick implementation assistance:</p>
<ul data-start="46294" data-end="47200">
<li data-start="46294" data-end="46493">
<p data-start="46296" data-end="46493"><em data-start="46296" data-end="46493">“Switch Square API from sandbox to production: use `connect.squareup.com` and the production access token when `process.env.NODE_ENV === 'production'`<span class="" data-state="closed"><span class="ms-1 inline-flex max-w-full items-center relative top-[-0.094rem] animate-[show_150ms_ease-in]"><a href="https://developer.squareup.com/docs/build-basics/general-considerations/using-rest-api#:~:text=,path%20after%20the%20host%20name" target="_blank" rel="noopener" alt="https://developer.squareup.com/docs/build-basics/general-considerations/using-rest-api#:~:text=,path%20after%20the%20host%20name" class="flex h-4.5 overflow-hidden rounded-xl px-2 text-[9px] font-medium text-token-text-secondary! bg-[#F4F4F4]! dark:bg-[#303030]! transition-colors duration-150 ease-in-out"><span class="relative start-0 bottom-0 flex h-full w-full items-center"><span class="flex h-4 w-full items-center justify-between overflow-hidden" style="opacity: 1; transform: none;"><span class="max-w-full grow truncate overflow-hidden text-center">developer.squareup.com</span></span></span></a></span></span>.”</em></p>
</li>
<li data-start="46494" data-end="46643">
<p data-start="46496" data-end="46643"><em data-start="46496" data-end="46643">“Add role verification in auth middleware: if `req.user.role !== 'admin'` for admin routes, return 403<span class="" data-state="closed"><span class="ms-1 inline-flex max-w-full items-center relative top-[-0.094rem] animate-[show_150ms_ease-in]"><a href="https://stackoverflow.com/questions/45201363/how-to-distinguish-between-user-types-when-authenticating-with-jwt#:~:text=2,For%20example" target="_blank" rel="noopener" alt="https://stackoverflow.com/questions/45201363/how-to-distinguish-between-user-types-when-authenticating-with-jwt#:~:text=2,For%20example" class="flex h-4.5 overflow-hidden rounded-xl px-2 text-[9px] font-medium text-token-text-secondary! bg-[#F4F4F4]! dark:bg-[#303030]! transition-colors duration-150 ease-in-out"><span class="relative start-0 bottom-0 flex h-full w-full items-center"><span class="flex h-4 w-full items-center justify-between overflow-hidden" style="opacity: 1; transform: none;"><span class="max-w-full grow truncate overflow-hidden text-center">stackoverflow.com</span></span></span></a></span></span>.”</em></p>
</li>
<li data-start="46644" data-end="46786">
<p data-start="46646" data-end="46786"><em data-start="46646" data-end="46786">“Implement server-side validation for inputs (email format, amount range) using express-validator<span class="" data-state="closed"><span class="ms-1 inline-flex max-w-full items-center relative top-[-0.094rem] animate-[show_150ms_ease-in]"><a href="https://cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/Input_Validation_Cheat_Sheet.html#:~:text=Input%20validation%20is%20performed%20to,received%20from%20the%20external%20party" target="_blank" rel="noopener" alt="https://cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/Input_Validation_Cheat_Sheet.html#:~:text=Input%20validation%20is%20performed%20to,received%20from%20the%20external%20party" class="flex h-4.5 overflow-hidden rounded-xl px-2 text-[9px] font-medium text-token-text-secondary! bg-[#F4F4F4]! dark:bg-[#303030]! transition-colors duration-150 ease-in-out"><span class="relative start-0 bottom-0 flex h-full w-full items-center"><span class="flex h-4 w-full items-center justify-between overflow-hidden" style="opacity: 1; transform: none;"><span class="max-w-full grow truncate overflow-hidden text-center">cheatsheetseries.owasp.org</span></span></span></a></span></span>.”</em></p>
</li>
<li data-start="46787" data-end="46940">
<p data-start="46789" data-end="46940"><em data-start="46789" data-end="46940">“On gift card redemption endpoint, ensure the code belongs to the authenticated merchant and hasn’t been redeemed, then mark as redeemed atomically.”</em></p>
</li>
<li data-start="46941" data-end="47073">
<p data-start="46943" data-end="47073"><em data-start="46943" data-end="47073">“Wrap the email sending logic in a try/catch and on failure, log error and flag gift card for retry (do not crash the request).”</em></p>
</li>
<li data-start="47074" data-end="47200">
<p data-start="47076" data-end="47200"><em data-start="47076" data-end="47200">“Remove or disable any test-mode shortcuts (like skipping payments or using test emails) when `NODE_ENV` is production.”</em></p>
</li>
</ul>
<p data-start="47202" data-end="47363" data-is-only-node="">By executing the above fixes and checks, all major blockers should be resolved, paving the way for a successful production deployment.
